<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1040641197150044200 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1040641197150044200><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, November 11, 2022 11:56 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1040641197150044200>11/11/2022 11:56 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I had a question for my department&#39;s leadership about how our customers and data providers have little insight into the resources required to provide them products or to deal with systems changes.

My leader&#39;s response was that our customers shouldn&#39;t have to worry about resourcing and capacity when making requests; they should focus on what&#39;s necessary for the business, and it&#39;s more or less on our management team to prioritize and evaluate feasibility.

My personal feeling is that if data teams&#39; output is &quot;free,&quot; the business will always overconsume. &quot;Nice-to-haves&quot; become &quot;essential&quot; and &quot;eventually&quot; becomes &quot;urgent&quot;; I&#39;ve personally sunk several sprints into &quot;essential&quot; and &quot;urgent&quot; work that the business ultimately didn&#39;t need or want.

Where do you all fall on this divide? I know what my first instinct is, but I acknowledge that the other philosophy is completely valid.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Friday, November 11, 2022 11:56 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1044609223415308338 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1044609223415308338><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/203043150753824768/89cca809b927b1b05a1bc003dc6a84ef.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/539458190782234634/20dfea0760f1ab515415443f2c288393.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=second_dose>Second Dose</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1044607883821719644')"> Here we studying for data engineering... Flink and spark we are learning both </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=jmcanboy data-user-id=203043150753824768>jmcanboy | talk less build more</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, November 22, 2022 10:44 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1044609223415308338>11/22/2022 10:44 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I am aware,  i think you just mid understood what I meant.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1044673502793437184 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1044673502793437184><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/567310952895217688/f324983e95815f688994d18c83b2914b.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/539458190782234634/20dfea0760f1ab515415443f2c288393.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=second_dose>Second Dose</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1044530884092629055')"> Why we need to use spark instead of flink </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=feeneckis data-user-id=567310952895217688>feeneckis</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, November 22, 2022 2:59 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1044673502793437184>11/22/2022 2:59 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I can speak from experience, where I&#39;m using Spark, specifically pyspark. It has some really great APIs that make it very easy to switch from batch to stream processing (Structured Streaming) just about all of the batch methods work in the streaming context. Further, they&#39;ve built out the pandas-on-spark API quite a bit, so you can define transformations in pandas that get run in a streaming context, so the time to get up and running for someone who has a python background is very fast. It also has nice way to guarantee exactly-once processing and if you have an API or endpoint that doesn&#39;t have a built in connector, the forEachBatch method makes it easy to process a stream as if it were a batch (since that&#39;s what Spark does anyways).

That said, although I haven&#39;t personally tested it, my understanding is that Flink would be better in cases where you need very low latency and/or processing of each record as it arrives. Structured Streaming has been improving, but it typically still has latency in the 1-2s range because it processes records as mini-batches, so not true real time processing. From what I&#39;ve seen, Spark docs say that they focus on Throughput (i.e. pushing massive volume of records in low amount of time) vs Latency (processing time per record), but I haven&#39;t seen that.

A caveat: I&#39;ve never used Flink, this is just my understanding and experience with Spark. So Flink may also have many of these features now.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1044675899234201670 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1044675899234201670><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/539458190782234634/20dfea0760f1ab515415443f2c288393.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/567310952895217688/f324983e95815f688994d18c83b2914b.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=feeneckis>feeneckis</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1044673502793437184')"> I can speak from experience, where I&#39;m using Spark, specifically pyspark. The short answer is that yes, GDPR can be a very central part of DE work in European-aimed businesses</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1044881396830834759 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1044881396830834759><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, November 23, 2022 4:45 AM">4:45 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>There are several areas to touch on:
<ul><li>Data access and logging the reason data is used</li><li>Privacy and masking/anonymization/removal of data</li><li>Consumer extract tooling</li><li>Right-to-be-forgotten request handling for all datasets</li><li>Retention of data and automatic removal of data after hitting the end of life

Obviously a lot of this comes down to having extremely strict requirements for metadata and building out robust catalogs that have enough information to do those things. The logging of purpose of use also can be a challenge as you need to tightly design and control business roles</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, November 23, 2022 4:46 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

I have a question for any Databricks heads out there.

Databricks &quot;infers&quot; dbfs for it&#39;s own tools. So if you have something like this works: <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">spark.load.json(&quot;/data/file.json&quot;)</code>, then with non-Databricks tools you need to prepend <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">/dbfs/</code>. So for example, this will return <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">False</code>:  <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pathlib.Path(&quot;/data/file.json&quot;).is_file()</code> but this will return <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">True</code> (assuming the file exists):  <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pathlib.Path(&quot;/dbfs/data/file.json&quot;)</code></span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1046356920849661963 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1046356920849661963><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105332965977944064/a3f1c0674bd7d1e2c448aa3431f34fc3.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=julmust data-user-id=105332965977944064>Julmust</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, November 27, 2022 6:28 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1046356920849661963>11/27/2022 6:28 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I&#39;m trying to plan a work event around advent of code for my team of 6 engineers. The idea is to get people to go outside of their comfort zone and use a language we don&#39;t normally use (thinking Go). 

The event is fully optional to take part in so I&#39;m considering turning it into a competition of some kind. I hope that will decrease the pressure to take part. However, I&#39;m not sure how to judge the competition. Because we have people who have done some development in Go and we have others who have never touched it. Doesn&#39;t seem fair to judge them on the same criteria. 

Has anyone else done anything similar at their company? How did you work around the knowledge gap?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1046371689585455106 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1046371689585455106><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/428959076052107265/ce548efe6e954d0648078e506d2c12ca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=labrex. data-user-id=428959076052107265>Labrex</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, November 27, 2022 7:27 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1046371689585455106>11/27/2022 7:27 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>If you talk about knowledge gap, i also had that problem. And still being a problem till now.
i had similar experience and not working as expected. Because, every people had their own interest. People with clear motivation and know what to do will grow itself. 
Using money or apreciation as a prize will goes to certain person (due to small team size), which still imbalance in terms of knowledge gap.

Now, i step back by trying to talk more, to know their interest and keep them enthusiasm.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1046377994962354256 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1046377994962354256><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105332965977944064/a3f1c0674bd7d1e2c448aa3431f34fc3.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=julmust data-user-id=105332965977944064>Julmust</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, November 27, 2022 7:52 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1046377994962354256>11/27/2022 7:52 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Yeah I want to make the competition as fair as possible. We&#39;re all decent programmers but some people are, naturally, better at it. 

My current idea is to use completion percentage within the first 24 hours as the primary scoring system, overall completion percentage as the first tiebreaker, and then a straight lottery draw as the second. There&#39;s a chance that everyone ends up on the same number of points but at least it means that a junior dev has (roughly) the same chance of winning as a senior. And the main idea is to get everyone to code and learn. 

And the prize will be small enough that it won&#39;t cause any friction (I&#39;m thinking a small trophy and a €50 gift card)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

I&#39;m not trying to tell you what tool is best for your purpouses but keep in mind that just because a tool is different, doesn&#39;t make it worse. In my mind disqualifying a tool because it&#39;s different is a slippery slope to answering the question &quot;Why?&quot; with &quot;Because it&#39;s how we&#39;ve always done things&quot;.

Again, not accusing anyone here of having that mindset but I once had a new colleague tell me, and this is a direct quote, &quot;I&#39;m too old to learn new things&quot;. He was one year older than me. (And didn&#39;t last very long in the company)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

All three sub-disciplines (platform, movement, analytics) are dealing with complex systems or ever-shifting inputs and outputs. You definitely should have some new project work, but a lot of your time is maintaining and iterating on existing solutions.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1053928293482627086 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1053928293482627086><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/222069360297115648/5990350e4c28af1a8cbb4165552549f2.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=mirage.ragnarok data-user-id=222069360297115648>Mirage / Fluff</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, December 18, 2022 3:54 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1053928293482627086>12/18/2022 3:54 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Views are generally best-practice for reporting. Some use-cases: 
1. For analyzing data, may need some calculations/joins. Use a view so business users don&#39;t need to do it (and reduce risk of them incorrectly doing so) in their tool.
2. Not all columns may want to be exposed, or relevant for BI analysis.
3. You may want to rename columns so they&#39;re more readable. E.g. cnv_fctr -&gt; ConversionFactor/conversion_factor
4. Can maintain the same schema since it&#39;s just a query, even if underlying table structure changes (e.g. modifying a DB column name, adding new columns to underlying tables, etc.).</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=100><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=💯 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f4af.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>5</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1056700073779679262 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1056700073779679262><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/5.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/322720507403436034/fa60be092eccb8e206c0c137adb4eacb.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=mill1>milli</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1056178423472586762')"> For landing the data into snowflake I use Snowpipe + a variety of tools to land into S3, and occasionally Kafka if it makes sense.

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1057704650033332245 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1057704650033332245><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/673255739623473164/4e424e301c3adff72d67c08c0a6f4eb0.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=armslegshandsfeet>armslegshandsfeet</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1057477079446331392')"> Can someone help me understand what &quot;pipelines&quot; are as divorced from data modeling and analytics? I have a super hard time understanding how entire teams are still spending effort to get tables out of a MySQL backend and into Snowflake. Like, isn&#39;t that a solved problem at this point? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=briancrant data-user-id=673255739623473164>briancrant</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, December 28, 2022 2:00 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1057704650033332245>12/28/2022 2:00 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I think the solved part of “pipeline” problems is the ingress/egress to/from enterprise SAAS tools. I can’t think of many cases where it makes more sense to roll your own than to use a Fivetran, etc. 

The lion’s share of what I think of as pipeline work is egress from application databases. Sure, there are some solved problems in this space like change data capture for MySQL and PostgreSQL dbs and tooling like Airflow for orchestration, but large scale applications are constantly evolving and pipelines need to evolve with them. Regardless of org structure and whether there are business analysts or data analysts to model the data and capture the business value, I don’t foresee pipeline work going anywhere. 

There are many great solutions for batch pipeline work, the streaming side of that equation is still in its early days and will require pipeline-esque work to reach maturity.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1057705210417528902 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1057705210417528902><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/499104423872823298/1a01884db1516a1f0a2fa9a48ed24947.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=armslegshandsfeet>armslegshandsfeet</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1057477079446331392')"> Can someone help me understand what &quot;pipelines&quot; are as divorced from data modeling and analytics? I have a super hard time understanding how entire teams are still spending effort to get tables out of a MySQL backend and into Snowflake. Like, isn&#39;t that a solved problem at this point? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=winenose data-user-id=499104423872823298>Lauri</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, December 28, 2022 2:02 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1057705210417528902>12/28/2022 2:02 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It&#39;s not. For example, one of our production tables <strong>can not</strong> be transported to data warehouse as is.
It has tens of millions of records, most of which get hundreds or thousands of updates per day.
So it&#39;s too big to full load, the change-data-capture itself is too big, and even pulling only latest updates is too big.
So it&#39;s quite a lot of (non-coding) work to re-architect the thing at source somehow.

It&#39;s a 99/1 principle - almost everything is solved, but the last bit takes a lot of effort.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1057708065144709180 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1057708065144709180><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/499104423872823298/1a01884db1516a1f0a2fa9a48ed24947.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=winenose data-user-id=499104423872823298>Lauri</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, December 28, 2022 2:14 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1057708065144709180>12/28/2022 2:14 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Or in my last place we were pulling some data out of binary files into JSON, to be queried later. It was nicely partitioned and people knew how to write queries, but the data size got too large. It also started to cost a lot. 
We could have added a level of partitioning, but it would not have helped cost.

So we had one of our special devs (stereotypical ultra geek) rewrite the binary parser to produce Parquet files instead. Took him a couple of months as it was a proper complex multi-threaded high throughput thingie.
End result - 10x smaller file size on average and all the other systems stayed working.

Another one of those 99/1 cases that still need to be done.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1057903687965626418 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1057903687965626418><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/5.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=paxos7775 data-user-id=1038924343415148566>Paxos</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, December 29, 2022 3:11 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1057903687965626418>12/29/2022 3:11 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Wanting to get some feedback for an article I&#39;m writing regarding development of highly performant, robust, and understandable data pipelines. Here are the qualities I can think of at the moment:
<ul><li>prefer CDC approaches to ETL / ELT</li><li>avoid managing too many responsibilities within a pipeline</li><li>prefer loading only data necessary to accomplish the function of the pipeline</li><li>always offload computation to a service different from the orchestrator </li><li>prefer performing data quality checks on incremental data instead of whole-table checks when possible</li><li>ensure pipeline tasks are atomic</li><li>ensure pipelines are idempotent</li><li>always perform quality checks on upstream sources</li><li>avoid direct communication between pipelines</li><li>always colocate docs with source code</li><li>try to develop pipelines that adhere to the separation of concerns principal</li><li>have built in functionality for data reprocessing in your pipelines


Would be curious to hear y&#39;all&#39;s thoughts on the above + any other points or design practices I may be missing.</li></ul></span></div></div></div></div></div>
